<Rating>4<//Rating>< review>
It's not actually a thousand steps, for anyone wondering. It's more like 200-300.
I went with a few friends and we climbed all the way down and complained about how it was too easy, only to be absolutely murdered climbing all the way back up.

The water is absolutely beautiful and it wasn't very crowded, though I did go on a Monday. Mileage may vary for the weekend.< /review>

< Review>
One of my favorite beaches in Southern California. Usually crowded during the summer but not in comparison to Newport or Santa Monica. Great place to spend the day or just enjoy the sunset. Make sure you save some energy to make your way back up the stairs at the end of your visit because going down is the easiest part. Parking is not easily accessible so make sure to use caution in the available areas due to traffic. Depending on the tide you might be able to explore the sea cave.

Keep the beach clean and remember to clean after yourself üöÆ‚ôªÔ∏è<//Review>

For those of you out there looking to enjoy the cave, it is against county law to do so, and extremely dangerous, I advise against this, and hope that you listen. First, they told her that they would not be able to look at her car until after the weekend (this was thursday) eh, okay... sure....
Friday morning they called her and told her that her tie rod end was broken (this I knew) but that her entire steering rack needed to be replaced because it was leaking, and repairs were  going to be $1,900. Now, this is a 2006 camry, car probably isnt worth 1,900 but I digress.
I called a mechanic in my area, asked him how much to replace our steering rack... He said $400 out the door.
So here comes the fun, the wife called and let them know that we were going to come pick up the car... They started to get weird. Wanted to know why, so she told them we got a better quote. They wanted to know how much, so when she said "400" they thought she meant 400 less than their quote... So now, oh guess what.. "well, we could probably go with cheaper parts... and get it down 300-350 less, but just so you know if you take it somewhere else they are probably going to blah blah" Trying everything they could to get her to keep it with them.
First of all, if you could have done it for cheaper, that should have been stated RIGHT AWAY. Not when we decide to take the car somewhere else.
So I get there to pick the car up, and there is no sign of leaking fluid ANYWHERE. Okay, maybe they just put it here? Started the car, still no leaks.
Got the car home, lifted it, and found that it had a broken tie rod as they stated... but absolutely NOTHING wrong with the steering rack. No leaks, no noise...
What was broken, though, was a lower control arm... which they did not mention. I mean, it was clear as day when I got under the car. So I have a feeling they did not even lift the car to actually inspect it. Or, if they did... they missed a major issue which is equally as bad.
So now, they quoted me 1900 to do the steering rack/alignment/tie rod ends.
What the car actually needed: inner tie rod, lower control arm, ball joint.
What I actually paid an honest mechanic: 150 in parts, 150 in labor.
The car is running just as it was before the accident. No issues with the steering rack, no leaking  power steering fluid. And the other mechanic actually pulled the dents out on his own, free of charge.
Please, be careful of predatory mechanics... These guys saw a woman who was desperate to get her car fixed, and jumped on the opportunity to make a quick buck for very little work.
Now, a week later the car is still fine, no leaking power steering fluid, no problems at all with the steering rack. I paid 100 dollars for a diagnosis, and got an incorrect assessment of what was wrong.  And had I not intervened, my wife would have paid the 1900 for 300$ worth of work.</review>< user>

<Rate>5<//Rate><review>Great little sweets shop, run by a very enthusiastic and generous couple. Their mochi selection includes typically the gyuuhi soft type and the red or white bean filled daifuku. Our favorites are the citrus and pineapple ones and the smooth redbean filled. They also have seasonal selection such as strawberry daifuku, or specially decorated pieces, or other forms of wagashi like kimi shigure, manju, or yokan.

<name>Cynthia Vo</name><Response>None</Response><Text>it took me 6 months before I could experience this shop for myself. I saw a post online about this shop and immediately forwarded to my friends locally, so they could check it out before I visited.

cash only, and business owners who are here to help their community as well. their selection is limited during pandemic, so I asked for one of everything they had. and then some ;)

my friend'a favorites are the chewy, milky, and peanut butter.

my favorites? PINEAPPLE MOCHI, I was amazed at how good it was, and both pieces I ate had a little bit of pineapple pulp, perfect. Chewy mochi, firmer, and chewy, with a slight saltiness I craved while trying all their other sweet flavors. Kinako (roasted soybean powder) was filled with the chunky sweet red bean, I liked their smooth red bean but the kinako powder is so tasty. Cute turtle dorayaki was a pancake with red bean filling. And the mochi wrapped in the pancake was also very good!! I had a SURPRISE when I bit into a filled mochi that had white bean filling and a dried apricot! it was sooo good. And finally, their yokan was super tall, def try it if you like red bean and agar.<//Text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOmtprGW_4mMZzOX7l4un6PbTsTLDwcC-iJWvE=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics></record></dataset><record>

<rate>5<//rate>< text>
Open Wednesday through Saturday, and as of my visit mochi are $1.85 each.

These mochi were delicious, and beautifully made! The plain mochi (pink and yellow stripe in pictures) was fresh, delicately chewy, and lightly fluffy---the perfect mochi consistency for my taste!

I recommend calling before you go in, to make sure they are open and check product availability. There are some beverages and various Asian snacks available as well in the small storefront.  The owners are around 70, and the thought that they might retire some day makes me sad, as I just found them and need them in my future forever.< /text>

< Review>
Hogetsu Bakery is a cute little husband and wife owned japanese bakery. The mochi they have here, which her husband hand makes, is very soft, cutely shaped, and delicious; they come plain, filled with red bean, or filled with white bean. I enjoy all three varieties but my favorites are definitely the white bean filled shaped mochi however, it's different for each person. The white bean mochi have a delicate and slightly sweet flavor; they are very well made, you can tell a lot of time and passion goes into making them.</Review>

I have to give a star to give a review.  If I could I'd give no stars at all. So I've been curious to try these desserts. <text>A friend and I needed a cheap place to crash in the city, this place beat out even the cheapest of motels by a large margin. Check in was quick and painless for two guys who walked in off the street. They said they preferred reservations, but they were not mandatory. My friend was new to the hostel experience and was unsure about the idea be after some "light nudging" we managed to convince him to stay. The hostel is split into Male and female dorms with private rooms of you wanted to spend a bit more. Beds were nice enough and blankets were more than adequate. Pancake mix and other foods were provided the next morning free of charge. Overall a good stay, with some very chill people. My only complaint is that the make dorm had female toilets making them difficult to use without "touching". Aside from that it has a nice view of a nearby island and the surrounding area. < Text>
Initially I had a hard time locating this hostel but with the patience of my Uber driver and limited directions from the hostel receptionist, I found my home away from home. The views from this hostel are truly incredible, nothing more magical than watching the sunset or sunrise from Angels Gate Park just a few feet away from your doorstep. Although the location is beautiful, I wouldn't recommend this hostel to a traveler on foot. Public transportation is scarce but available. I had to rely a lot on Uber's which adds up fairly quickly so keep that in mind fellow backpackers. But there still is a lot to do/see/eat that is in walking distance!

The space was clean, friendly staff, and a decent breakfast provided. The price per night is a bit high in my opinion but I enjoyed my stay nonetheless.</Text>

Dr Wong has been attending my family for years. <resp>None<//resp>< text>
There is no reason I can see in this great universe of ours how I actually got to see Dr. Kevin for the first time. Except perhaps "good luck" and some sort of Master Plan. I don't live in the Bay Area. I currently live in Hyderabad, India. But due to our various travels, I found myself in October of 2012 in San Francisco..and in a great deal of pain. Dr. Kevin came highly recommended from a friend in the area...and he was able to squeeze me (and my wife!) in with very short notice.

Dr. Kevin is not just a chiropractor.. he is a healer. And he genuinely cares about his patients. The treatments, orthotics, exercise plan (and the tennis-ball trick!) I received at Orinda Chiropractic got me squared-away and able to get on the plane for a pain-free 30-hour journey back to India. And another year and a half of golf!

But beside the treatments and the caring... it was the advice I received. Dr Kevin was straight with me and said that unless I lost weight and changed my lifestyle, my condition would only worsen and become more crippling. I took his word for it.

By November of 2013, I had lost 35 kgs and I owe much of the kick-start to Dr Kevin Wong!

By December, however... my new active lifestyle was beginning to take its toll. I saw an orthopedic surgeon here in India... and a RTHR (right total hip replacement) surgery was indicated. I wrote to Dr Wong for his advice. I received an instant reply with more sage advice, some congratulations for losing the weight...and his blessing for getting the surgery done. He assured me that it was going to be for the best in my case, and reassured me that not all western medicine is a bad thing... and that these types of surgeries usually delivered a greatly-improved lifestyle.

I am now Day Six Post Op and feeling great. I am up and around the house on a walker....and may be on a one-arm cane at the end of 30-days. Doing the physical therapy is not easy, but I have no choice. I am still in India and will be for the next 72 days, when we return to the U.S. for good.... we will be in Salt Lake City, Utah.

And that's only a short flight away... because Dr. Kevin is, and will always be, my chiropractor!< /text>

<name>Eileen Tien (Áî∞ËâæËåπ)<//name>< Text>
When I was kid in Taiwan, my parents used to take us to those shabu and BBQ kind of restaurant.
They all have similar names... Kariya, Coriya, Cariya, Karaya and that sort.

It is an all you can eat restaurant. There are 3 options.
For $13.99 you can order beef, pork, intestine, pork blood, etc.
The next level (I think $18) includes seafood.
The most expensive (I think $20 something) option includes higher quality beef and lamb.
The all you can eat also includes all marinated meat for BBQ and vegetables.
We think the cheapest option is enough food.
You can also choose a soup base for the shabu shabu.
Eating with Dr. P meaning we are getting the spicy soup base.
The spicy soup base is more like a Taiwanese style soup base.

While waiting for the food to arrive, we headed to the sauce bar to make our dipping sauce.
Our first bowl of dipping sauce was not good.
We didn't know their garlic soy sauce was super sweet.
My favorite dipping sauce for spicy hot pot is simply vinegar + sesame oil + green onion + garlic.

Next to the sauce bar, there are also some cooked food.
There were soup, egg rolls, rice, and chow mein.
And they have Taiwanese minced pork rice!!
We got a bowl, and it was good!

We like the shabu shabu. I was very happy that intestine and pork blood was included.
The meat quality was decent. Vegetables were fresh.
The marinated BBQ meat wasn't bad, but we definitely enjoyed the shabu shabu part more.

This is not a fancy restaurant. But you definitely will leave here very full.
Service was good. The waitress was very attentive, and kept checking to see if we need anything.
Was it the best shabu shabu? No. Was it the best BBQ? No.
But hey, you can get shabu shabu and BBQ at the same time for cheap!<//Text>

<user_id>101723197147665229687< /user_id><username>Natalie K< /username><Date>1421380489633</Date><rate>3</rate>< review>
I feel horrible for not giving this place more stars because they were so nice to us but the BBQ just really wasn't great. In fact, if not for the awesome service, I would have probably given this place 2 stars.

At Kariya, for the rock bottom price of $11, you can get AYCE Korean BBQ and Shabu Shabu. Yes, you read that right. It's $11 for AYCE BBQ and Shabu Shabu at the same time. For this price, you also get access to the food bar, which has egg rolls, chow mein, fried rice, and a bunch of appetizer items.

The grill has a hot pot in the center and a round grill surrounding the pot for your BBQ. You can cook both at once.

The hot pot is decent although the options of sauces could be better. The real disappointing part though is the KBBQ. It's clear that they're not Korean at all. The menu and all the employees are Chinese. The meat quality is poor and the only side dish they serve with your BBQ is kimchi.

If you want to come here, I would recommend just spending $11 to eat cheap AYCE hot pot and skip the BBQ. We had a little bit of grilled meat and quickly resigned to just eating hot pot ourselves.< /review>

<gmap_id>0x80dd2da950db9395:0xa1cf94fb6315b446</gmap_id>< Text>
$9.99, me love you long time!

I was invited by my buddy, Janel, for dinner with her & her peeps at Kariya Shabu Shabu & BBQ.  Not one to pass up $9.99 AYCE meat at a restaurant that A)I haven't been to & B)is closeby, my daily horoscope said "You shall soon be accumulating bad karma by devouring animals."  Wow, how'd they know?!?

On a Friday night, Kariya was on & popping.

Meal options are $9.99/$14.99 & $17.99.  $9.99 includes brisket, chicken leg meat, pork, pork belly, pork blood, pork intestine, pork kidney, pork liver & beef tripe.  Available add-on's for no extra charge are-

Marinated meats-brisket, spicy garlic chicken, pork & pork belly

Vegetables etc. - fish balls, beef balls, squid balls, imitation crab, napa cabbage, chinese lettuce, spinach, cabbage, bak choy, turnip, sweet corn, bamboo shoots, mushrooms, pumpkin, onions, sweet potato, taro, fried & fresh tofu, tofu skin, tomatoes & winter melon.

Noodles-egg noodles, vermicelli, bean noodles, thin rice noodles, HK wonton, dumplings & Taiwanese minced pork rice.

Choice of soup base - Kariya house special soup, special hot & spicy soup, Japanese coconut curry soup, plain seaweed soup, Japanese miso soup or House vegetarian tomato soup

After choosing what you want, commence with the cooking-

Kariya has a self serve sauce section, for dipping and/or soup

Fried rice, white rice & tapioca dessert are also self serve.

The various meat selections we had were good, especially the brisket, kidneys & liver.

The owner even let us have complimentary marinated salmon.  Nice!

Seating includes booths & tables, some just for shabu shabu.
Reservations can be made for groups of 10 or more, which is great because Kariya was quite busy.  Parking is in a private lot shared by Formosan Restaurant, Hong Kong Tropical fish etc.

We had a lot of food, but with my hollow leg, we managed to make Kariya lose money ;p

Kariya Shabu Shabu & BBQ, I'm a fan!  AYCE meat & veggies starting at $9.99, plus great service, have won me over to your establishment.  I can't wait to come back for another meat coma!

Highly recommend!
NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM</Text>
